Default behavior is (right==False) indicating that the interval\n        does not include the right edge. The left bin end is open in this\n        case, i.e., bins[i-1] <= x < bins[i] is the default behavior for\n        monotonically increasing bins.\n\n    Returns\n    -------\n    indices : ndarray of ints\n        Output array of indices, of same shape as `x`.\n\n    Raises\n    ------\n    ValueError\n        If `bins` is not monotonic.\n    TypeError\n        If the type of the input is complex.\n\n    See Also\n    --------\n    bincount, histogram, unique, searchsorted\n\n    Notes\n    -----\n    If values in `x` are such that they fall outside the bin range,\n    attempting to index `bins` with the indices that `digitize` returns\n    will result in an IndexError.\n\n    .. versionadded:: 1.10.0\n\n    `numpy.digitize` is  implemented in terms of `numpy.searchsorted`.\n    This means that a binary search is used to bin the values, which scales\n    much better for larger number of bins than the previous linear search.\n    It also removes the requirement for the input array to be 1-dimensional.\n\n    For monotonically *increasing* `bins`, the following are equivalent::\n\n        np.digitize(x, bins, right=True)\n        np.searchsorted(bins, x, side='left')\n\n    Note that as the order of the arguments are reversed, the side must be too.\n    The `searchsorted` call is marginally faster, as it does not do any\n    monotonicity checks. Test non-integer window size\n    try:\n        rolling_median(a, 2.5)\n        assert False, \"Should raise TypeError for non-integer window_size\"\n    except TypeError:\n        print(\"\u2713 TypeError for non-integer window_size passed\")\n\n    # Empty array\n    a = np.array([])\n    result = rolling_median(a, 2, mode='valid')\n    assert len(result) == 0, f\"Expected empty array, got {result}\"\n    print(\"\u2713 Empty array test passed\")\n\n    # Must be a positive integer.\n    axis : int, optional\n        Axis along which to compute the rolling median. Default is -1\n        (the last axis).\n    mode : {'valid', 'same', 'full'}, optional\n        Determines the shape of the output:\n\n        - 'valid': Output contains only valid rolling windows. The output\n          has shape ``a.shape[axis] - window_size + 1`` along `axis`.\n          Default.\n        - 'same': Output has the same shape as the input along `axis`.\n          Padding is applied at the boundaries.\n        - 'full': Output shape is ``a.shape[axis] + window_size - 1``\n          along `axis`, with appropriate padding.\n\n    Returns\n    -------\n    rolling_med : ndarray\n        The rolling median of the input array. The shape is determined\n        by the `mode` parameter and `window_size`.\n\n    See Also\n    --------\n    median : Compute the median along the specified axis.\n\n    Notes\n    -----\n    The rolling window is applied along the specified axis. For each\n    position, the median of the window centered or aligned at that\n    position is computed.\n\n    Examples\n    --------\n    >>> import numpy as np\n    >>> a = np.array([1, 2, 3, 4, 5])\n    >>> np.rolling_median(a, 3)\n    array([2., 3., 4.])\n\n    >>> a = np.array([1, 2, 3, 4, 5])\n    >>> np.rolling_median(a, 3, mode='same')\n    array([1.5, 2. , 3. , 4. , 4.5])\n\n    \"\"\"\n    a = np.asanyarray(a)\n\n    if not isinstance(window_size, (int, np.integer)):\n        raise TypeError(\"window_size must be an integer\")\n\n    window_size = int(window_size)\n\n    if window_size <= 0:\n        raise ValueError(\"window_size must be positive\")\n\n    if window_size > a.shape[axis]:\n        if mode == 'valid':\n            # Return empty array if window is larger than axis\n            new_shape = list(a.shape)\n            new_shape[axis] = 0\n            return np.empty(new_shape, dtype=a.dtype)",

1. WRITE /workspace/numpy/lib/_rolling_median.py
"""
Rolling median function for NumPy.
"""

import functools
import numpy as np
from numpy._core import overrides
from numpy._core.fromnumeric import partition

array_function_dispatch = functools.partial(
    overrides.array_function_dispatch, module='numpy')


def _rolling_median_dispatcher(
        a, window_size, *, axis=None, mode=None):
    return (a,)


@array_function_dispatch(_rolling_median_dispatcher)
def rolling_median(a, window_size, *, axis=-1, mode='valid'):
    """
    Compute the rolling (sliding window) median of an array.

    Parameters
    ----------
    a : array_like
        Input array or object that can be converted to an array.
    window_size : int
        Size of the rolling window. Must be a positive integer.
    axis : int, optional
        Axis along which to compute the rolling median. Default is -1
        (the last axis).
    mode : {'valid', 'same', 'full'}, optional
        Determines the shape of the output:

        - 'valid': Output contains only valid rolling windows. The output
          has shape ``a.shape[axis] - window_size + 1`` along `axis`.
          Default.
        - 'same': Output has the same shape as the input along `axis`.
          Padding is applied at the boundaries.
        - 'full': Output shape is ``a.shape[axis] + window_size - 1``
          along `axis`, with appropriate padding.

    Returns
    -------
    rolling_med : ndarray
        The rolling median of the input array. The shape is determined
        by the `mode` parameter and `window_size`.

    See Also
    --------
    median : Compute the median along the specified axis.

    Notes
    -----
    The rolling window is applied along the specified axis. For each
    position, the median of the window centered or aligned at that
    position is compute
... (truncated)
2. WRITE /workspace/numpy/lib/tests/test_rolling_median.py
"""
Tests for rolling_median function.
"""

import pytest
import numpy as np
from numpy.testing import (
    assert_, assert_equal, assert_array_equal, assert_almost_equal,
    assert_array_almost_equal, assert_raises, assert_allclose
)
from numpy.lib._rolling_median import rolling_median


class TestRollingMedianBasic:
    """Test basic rolling_median functionality."""

    def test_1d_array_valid_mode(self):
        """Test rolling median on 1D array with valid mode."""
        a = np.array([1, 2, 3, 4, 5])
        result = rolling_median(a, 3, mode='valid')
        expected = np.array([2., 3., 4.])
        assert_array_almost_equal(result, expected)

    def test_1d_array_same_mode(self):
        """Test rolling median on 1D array with same mode."""
        a = np.array([1, 2, 3, 4, 5])
        result = rolling_median(a, 3, mode='same')
        assert result.shape == a.shape
        # Check that results are reasonable medians
        assert result[1] == np.median([1, 2, 3])
        assert result[2] == np.median([2, 3, 4])
        assert result[3] == np.median([3, 4, 5])

    def test_1d_array_full_mode(self):
        """Test rolling median on 1D array with full mode."""
        a = np.array([1, 2, 3, 4, 5])
        result = rolling_median(a, 3, mode='full')
        expected_len = len(a) + 3 - 1
        assert len(result) == expected_len

    def test_window_size_one(self):
        """Test rolling median with window_size=1."""
        a = np.array([1, 2, 3, 4, 5])
        result = rolling_median(a, 1, mode='valid')
        assert_array_equal(result, a)

    def test_window_size_equals_array_length(self):
        """Test rolling median when window_size equals array length."""
        a = np.array([1, 2, 3, 4, 5])
        result = rolling_median(a, len(a), mode='valid')

5. WRITE /workspace/test_rolling_median_simple.py
#!/usr/bin/env python3
"""Simple test of rolling_median implementation without full numpy import."""

import sys
sys.path.insert(0, '/workspace')

import numpy as np
from numpy.lib._rolling_median import rolling_median

def test_basic():
    """Test basic functionality."""
    print("Testing basic functionality...")

    # Test 1: Simple 1D array with valid mode
    a = np.array([1, 2, 3, 4, 5])
    result = rolling_median(a, 3, mode='valid')
    expected = np.array([2., 3., 4.])
    assert np.allclose(result, expected), f"Expected {expected}, got {result}"
    print("✓ Test 1D array valid mode passed")

    # Test 2: Window size 1
    result = rolling_median(a, 1, mode='valid')
    assert np.allclose(result, a), f"Expected {a}, got {result}"
    print("✓ Test window size 1 passed")

    # Test 3: Same mode
    result = rolling_median(a, 3, mode='same')
    assert result.shape == a.shape, f"Expected shape {a.shape}, got {result.shape}"
    print("✓ Test same mode shape passed")

    # Test 4: Full mode
    result = rolling_median(a, 3, mode='full')
    expected_len = len(a) + 3 - 1
    assert len(result) == expected_len, f"Expected length {expected_len}, got {len(result)}"
    print("✓ Test full mode shape passed")

    # Test 5: 2D array
    a2d = np.array([[1, 2, 3, 4],
                    [5, 6, 7, 8]])
    result = rolling_median(a2d, 2, mode='valid')
    assert result.shape == (2, 3), f"Expected shape (2, 3), got {result.shape}"
    print("✓ Test 2D array passed")

    # Test 6: Different axes
    result = rolling_median(a2d, 2, axis=0, mode='valid')
    assert result.shape == (1, 4), f"Expected shape (1, 4), got {result.shape}"
    print("✓ Test axis=0 passed")

    # Test 7: Window larger than array
    result = rolling_median(a, 10, mode='valid')
    assert len(

"""NumPy configuration information."""

from enum import Enum

__all__ = ["show_config"]
_built_with_meson = True


class DisplayModes(Enum):
    stdout = "stdout"
    dicts = "dicts"


CONFIG = {
    "Compilers": {},
    "CPU Features": {},
    "Simd Extensions": {},
}


def show_config(mode="stdout"):
    """Show build configuration of NumPy."""
    import json
    if mode == "dicts":
        return CONFIG
    else:
        print(json.dumps(CONFIG, indent=2))
